  13. If you color your hair, you know how expensive it can be, and what a pain it can be to keep up with the colorings...especially if you're like me and color your hair auburn or red. It will fade. To help with this, you can actually extend the life of your colorings by using dry shampoo in between washings. If you're not a teenager and don't have super oily hair, you really don't need to wash it every single day. You really just need a refresh every other day or so. By using dry shampoo on the in-between days, you can double the life of your coloring. It won't do a thing for the roots, but it will stop half the fading you would normally get, which is what makes your roots show up so badly. I found this out when I got gout (of all things) and had to basin-bathe for a couple weeks (I know, I know) and had to use this on my hair because I just couldn't stand it (and literally, I couldn't stand up on my foot)...my hair was clean and smelled fresh, was soft and silky and I felt fine about it. Not to mention, I noticed that my red hair did not fade out. So I decided to tell my friends, family and colleagues...and now YOU...you should keep a can of this on hand. If you have long hair, like I do, it will last about 3 or 4 good &#34;shampooings&#34; but for $2, that isn't a bad deal. Plus, it's an awesome deal here on Amazon. Honestly, it's cheaper here than at my local drugstore. I've tried different Suave dry shampoos and they are all about the same for cleaning, but this one seems to add a luster that the others don't, possibly due to the keratin. Enjoy!

  16. I've spent a lot of money on different dry shampoos. This one is one of (if not) the cheapest I've bought and it works better than the others. Most cans I've purchased run out after four or five uses. This usually lasts about ten or more. I have shoulder length hair.<br /><br />TIP: As with ANY aerosol, don't hold the sprayer down. You'll end up using way more than you need to and running out faster. Spray in short quick bursts aiming where you need product. By holding it down, you're coating and recoating areas you've already hit. It's an easy way to ensure you use less product and hit only the areas you need to hit. This works for everything from spray paint to glass cleaner.<br /><br />As for the negative reviews...<br />- Some people say it doesn't last long. It lasts just as long as every other dry shampoo on the market. I've tried most. Try spraying \\"shots\\" of product instead of just holding the sprayer down like I mention above. This one is at least on par with other products. I think better.<br />- Some people have said the smell is nasty or overpowering. Makes me wonder how much they're using. I like the scent, it's floral, possibly a bit \\"old fashioned\\" smelling but it's not overpowering at all.<br />- Some people say it turns their hair grey especially noticeable on darker hair. If I notice that it seems to have lightened my fairly dark hair, I just brush my hair until it blends in. I mean... the reason this product works is because it's spraying a powder onto your hair. The powder absorbs oil. If you can see the powder on your hair, there's no oil to absorb and you didn't need to use it in the first place. Still I think most all hair is oily enough to absorb a reasonable amount. Try using less by spot spraying like I mentioned above and then go from there.<br />- Some people have said it changes the texture of their hair. I don't disagree with this. If you use too much it will probably dry your hair out. (Temporarily until you wash the product out of your hair.) It's a powder that's meant to absorb moisture so it's SUPPOSED to dry your hair out. It only makes sense that you shouldn't overdo it or you'll overdry your hair. Using this product makes my hair feel thicker and look \\"bigger.\\" It does feel a little dry, but not like straw as some have said.<br /><br />I think most of the problems people have with this product are due to overuse or not understanding the product to begin with. It's called a dry shampoo, but it is not washing your hair, it's just absorbing oil. Some of the residue can be brushed out, but the product definitely stays in your hair until you wash it with liquid shampoo and water. If you don't like this product, you're not going to like any dry shampoo. As far as dry shampoos go, this is one of, if not the best.

With other dry shampoos I've used in the past, I can simply finger-comb or tease my hair at the roots with my fingers to remove the cast. That's preferable to me because I usually use dry shampoo when I wake up late and need to be out the door!<br /><br />However, I'll say that this product definitely does what it promises and is a steal at this price. I bet it would work really well on people who have particularly oily scalps. Personally, though, I wouldn't repurchase because I prefer other dry shampoos I've tried.
